<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Turkish Empire" redirects here. .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Turkey" title="Template:History of Turkey"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Turkey" title="Template talk:History of Turkey"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Turkey&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Ottoman Empire</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="/É/: 'o' in 'body'">É</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/É/: 'a' in 'about'">É</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/É/: 'a' in 'about'">É</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ota">Ø¯ÙÙØª Ø¹ÙÙÙ Ø¹Ø«ÙØ§ÙÙÙ</span>, <small>romanized:Â </small><span title="Ottoman Turkish-language romanization"><i lang="ota-Latn">Devlet-i Ê¿AlÄ«ye-i Ê¿O<u>s</u>mÄnÄ«ye</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">OsmanlÄ± Ä°mparatorluÄu</i> or <span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">OsmanlÄ± Devleti</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Empire ottoman</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[e]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StraussConstp36_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-StraussConstp36-20">[16]</a></sup> also known as the <b>Turkish Empire</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[17]</a></sup> was an empire<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[f]</a></sup> that controlled much of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">Northern Africa</a> between the 14th and early 20th centuries. It was founded at the end of the 13th century in northwestern <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> in the town of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6%C4%9F%C3%BCt" title="SÃ¶ÄÃ¼t">SÃ¶ÄÃ¼t</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Bilecik_Province" title="Bilecik Province">Bilecik Province</a>) by the <a href="/wiki/Turkoman_(ethnonym)" title="Turkoman (ethnonym)">Turkoman</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-principality_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-principality-25">[19]</a></sup> tribal leader <a href="/wiki/Osman_I" title="Osman I">Osman I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[20]</a></sup> After 1354, the Ottomans crossed into Europe and, with the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe" title="Ottoman wars in Europe">conquest</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, the Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Anatolian_beyliks" title="Anatolian beyliks">beylik</a> was transformed into a transcontinental empire. The Ottomans ended the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">conquest of Constantinople</a> in 1453 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror" title="Mehmed the Conqueror">Mehmed the Conqueror</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Quataert2005_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Quataert2005-27">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>Under the reign of <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a>, the Ottoman Empire marked the peak of its power and prosperity, as well as the highest development of its governmental, social, and economic systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[22]</a></sup> At the beginning of the 17th century, the empire contained <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Administrative divisions of the Ottoman Empire">32 provinces</a> and numerous <a href="/wiki/Vassal_and_tributary_states_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Vassal and tributary states of the Ottoman Empire">vassal states</a>. Some of these were later absorbed into the Ottoman Empire, while others were granted various types of autonomy over the course of centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[g]</a></sup> With <a href="/wiki/History_of_Istanbul#Ottoman_Empire" title="History of Istanbul">Constantinople</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>) as its capital and control of lands around the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a>, the Ottoman Empire was at the centre of interactions between the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> for six centuries.
</p><p>While the empire was once thought to have entered a period of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_Decline_Thesis" title="Ottoman Decline Thesis">decline</a> following the death of Suleiman the Magnificent, this view is no longer supported by the majority of academic historians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-decline_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-decline-31">[24]</a></sup> The newer academic consensus posits that the empire continued to maintain a flexible and strong economy, society and military throughout the 17th and for much of the 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[25]</a></sup> However, during a long period of peace from 1740 to 1768, the Ottoman military system fell behind that of its European rivals, the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_monarchy" title="Habsburg monarchy">Habsburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian</a> empires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AksanOW_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-AksanOW-33">[26]</a></sup> The Ottomans consequently suffered severe military defeats in the late 18th and early 19th centuries. The successful <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">Greek War of Independence</a> concluded with <a href="/wiki/Decolonization#Ottoman_Empire" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> of Greece following the <a href="/wiki/London_Protocol_(1830)" title="London Protocol (1830)">London Protocol (1830)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Constantinople_(1832)" title="Treaty of Constantinople (1832)">Treaty of Constantinople (1832)</a>. This and other defeats prompted the Ottoman state to initiate a comprehensive process of reform and modernization known as the <a href="/wiki/Tanzimat" title="Tanzimat">Tanzimat</a>. Thus, over the course of the 19th century, the Ottoman state became vastly more powerful and organized internally, despite suffering further territorial losses, especially in the Balkans, where a number of new states emerged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress" title="Committee of Union and Progress">Committee of Union and Progress</a> (CUP) established the <a href="/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era" title="Second Constitutional Era">Second Constitutional Era</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a> in 1908, turning the Empire into a constitutional monarchy, which conducted <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Elections in the Ottoman Empire">competitive multi-party elections</a>. However, after the disastrous <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a>, the now radicalized and nationalistic CUP took over the government in the <a href="/wiki/1913_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1913 Ottoman coup d'Ã©tat">1913 coup d'Ã©tat</a>, creating a one-party regime. The CUP allied the Empire with <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a>, hoping to escape from the diplomatic isolation which had contributed to its recent territorial losses, and thus joined <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> on the side of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[28]</a></sup> While the Empire was able to largely hold its own during the conflict, it was struggling with internal dissent, especially with the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Revolt" title="Arab Revolt">Arab Revolt</a> in its Arabian holdings. During this time, the Ottoman government engaged in <a href="/wiki/Late_Ottoman_genocides" title="Late Ottoman genocides">genocide</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_genocide" title="Armenian genocide">Armenians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_genocide" title="Assyrian genocide">Assyrians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greek_genocide" title="Greek genocide">Greeks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[30]</a></sup> The Empire's defeat and the occupation of part of its territory by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied Powers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I" title="Aftermath of World War I">aftermath of World War I</a> resulted in <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Partition of the Ottoman Empire">its partitioning</a> and the loss of its Middle Eastern territories, which were <a href="/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement" title="SykesâPicot Agreement">divided between the United Kingdom and France</a>. The successful <a href="/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence" title="Turkish War of Independence">Turkish War of Independence</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal AtatÃ¼rk">Mustafa Kemal AtatÃ¼rk</a> against the occupying Allies, led to the emergence of the <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Republic of Turkey</a> in the Anatolian heartland and the <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_the_Ottoman_sultanate" title="Abolition of the Ottoman sultanate">abolition of the Ottoman monarchy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[31]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Names_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Names of the Ottoman Empire">Names of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Osman_I#Name" title="Osman I">Osman I Â§Â Name</a></div>
<p>The word <i>Ottoman</i> is a historical <a href="/wiki/Anglicisation" title="Anglicisation">anglicisation</a> of the name of <a href="/wiki/Osman_I" title="Osman I">Osman I</a>, the founder of the Empire and of the ruling <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_dynasty" title="Ottoman dynasty">House of Osman</a> (also known as the Ottoman dynasty). Osman's name in turn was the Turkish form of the Arabic name <span title="Ottoman Turkish (1500-1928)-language romanization"><i lang="ota-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Uthman_(name)" title="Uthman (name)">Ê¿UthmÄn</a></i></span> (<span title="Ottoman Turkish (1500-1928)-language text"><span dir="rtl" lang="ota-Arab">Ø¹Ø«ÙØ§Ù</span></span>). In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a>, the empire was referred to as <span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">Devlet-i Ê¿AlÄ«ye-yi Ê¿O<u>s</u>mÄnÄ«ye</i></span> (<span title="Ottoman Turkish (1500-1928)-language text"><span dir="rtl" lang="ota-Arab">Ø¯ÙÙØª Ø¹ÙÙÙ Ø¹Ø«ÙØ§ÙÛÙ</span></span>), literally "The Supreme Ottoman State", or alternatively <span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">Ê¿O<u>s</u>mÄnlÄ± Devleti</i></span> (<span title="Ottoman Turkish (1500-1928)-language text"><span dir="rtl" lang="ota-Arab">Ø¹Ø«ÙØ§ÙÙÙ Ø¯ÙÙØªÙ</span></span>). In <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Modern Turkish</a>, it is known as <span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">OsmanlÄ± Ä°mparatorluÄu</i></span> ("The Ottoman Empire") or <span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">OsmanlÄ± Devleti</i></span> ("The Ottoman State").<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The Turkish word for "Ottoman" (<span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">OsmanlÄ±</i></span>) originally referred to the tribal followers of Osman in the fourteenth century. The word subsequently came to be used to refer to the empire's military-administrative elite. In contrast, the term "Turk" (<span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">TÃ¼rk</i></span>) was used to refer to the Anatolian peasant and tribal population and was seen as a disparaging term when applied to urban, educated individuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: xxvi">:âxxviâ</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[33]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a>, an educated, urban-dwelling Turkish-speaker who was not a member of the military-administrative class would often refer to himself neither as an <span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">OsmanlÄ±</i></span> nor as a <span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">TÃ¼rk</i></span>, but rather as a <span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">RÅ«mÄ«</i></span> (<span title="Ottoman Turkish (1500-1928)-language text"><span dir="rtl" lang="ota-Arab">Ø±ÙÙÙ</span></span>), or "Roman", meaning an inhabitant of the territory of the former <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> in the Balkans and Anatolia. The term <span title="Turkish-language text"><i lang="tr">RÅ«mÄ«</i></span> was also used to refer to Turkish speakers by the other Muslim peoples of the empire and beyond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 11">:â11â</span></sup> As applied to Ottoman Turkish-speakers, this term began to fall out of use at the end of the seventeenth century, and instead of the word increasingly became associated with the Greek population of the empire, a meaning that it still bears in Turkey today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 51">:â51â</span></sup>
</p><p>In Western Europe, the names Ottoman Empire, Turkish Empire and Turkey were often used interchangeably, with Turkey being increasingly favoured both in formal and informal situations. This dichotomy was officially ended in 1920â1923, when the newly established <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey" title="Grand National Assembly of Turkey">Turkish government</a> chose Turkey as the sole official name. At present, most scholarly historians avoid the terms "Turkey", "Turks", and "Turkish" when referring to the Ottomans, due to the empire's multinational character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-43">[36]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="History of the Ottoman Empire">History of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Territorial evolution of the Ottoman Empire">Territorial evolution of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>
<h3><span id="Rise_.28c._1299.E2.80.931453.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_(c._1299â1453)">Rise (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">â1299â1453</span>)</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Rise of the Ottoman Empire">Rise of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Osman_I" title="Osman I">Osman I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_dynasty" title="Ottoman dynasty">Ottoman dynasty</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaza_Thesis" title="Gaza Thesis">Gaza Thesis</a></div>
<p>As the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum" title="Sultanate of Rum">Rum Sultanate</a> declined well into the 13th century, <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> was divided into a patchwork of independent Turkish principalities known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anatolian_Beyliks" title="Anatolian Beyliks">Anatolian Beyliks</a>. One of these beyliks, in the region of <a href="/wiki/Bithynia" title="Bithynia">Bithynia</a> on the frontier of the Byzantine Empire, was led by the Turkish tribal leader Osman I (<abbr title="died">d.</abbr> 1323/4), a figure of obscure origins from whom the name Ottoman is derived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 444">:â444â</span></sup> Osman's early followers consisted both of Turkish tribal groups and Byzantine renegades, with many but not all converts to Islam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 59">:â59â</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 127">:â127â</span></sup> Osman extended the control of his principality by conquering Byzantine towns along the <a href="/wiki/Sakarya_River" title="Sakarya River">Sakarya River</a>. A Byzantine defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bapheus" title="Battle of Bapheus">Battle of Bapheus</a> in 1302 contributed to Osman's rise as well. It is not well understood how the early Ottomans came to dominate their neighbors, due to the lack of sources surviving from this period. The <a href="/wiki/Ghaza_thesis" title="Ghaza thesis">Ghaza thesis</a> popular during the twentieth century credited their success to their rallying of religious warriors to fight for them in the name of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, but it is no longer generally accepted. No other hypothesis has attracted broad acceptance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 5, 10">:â5,â10â</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 104">:â104â</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2943" data-file-width="2018" decoding="async" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg/170px-Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg/255px-Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg/340px-Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nicopolis" title="Battle of Nicopolis">Battle of Nicopolis</a> in 1396, depicted in an <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_miniature" title="Ottoman miniature">Ottoman miniature</a> from 1523</div></div></div>
<p>In the century after the death of Osman I, Ottoman rule had begun to extend over Anatolia and the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Balkans" title="History of the Balkans">Balkans</a>. The earliest conflicts began during the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars" title="ByzantineâOttoman wars">ByzantineâOttoman wars</a>, waged in <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> in the late 13th century before entering Europe in the mid-14th century, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars" title="BulgarianâOttoman wars">BulgarianâOttoman wars</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars" title="SerbianâOttoman wars">SerbianâOttoman wars</a> waged beginning in the mid 14th century. Much of this period was characterised by <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Ottoman expansion into the Balkans</a>. Osman's son, <a href="/wiki/Orhan" title="Orhan">Orhan</a>, captured the northwestern Anatolian city of <a href="/wiki/Bursa" title="Bursa">Bursa</a> in 1326, making it the new capital of the Ottoman state and supplanting Byzantine control in the region. The important port city of <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a> was captured from the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venetians</a> in 1387 and sacked. The Ottoman victory in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Kosovo in 1389</a> effectively marked <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Serbian_Empire" title="Fall of the Serbian Empire">the end of Serbian power</a> in the region, paving the way for Ottoman expansion into Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 95â96">:â95â96â</span></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nicopolis" title="Battle of Nicopolis">Battle of Nicopolis</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire" title="Second Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian</a> <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Vidin" title="Tsardom of Vidin">Tsardom of Vidin</a> in 1396, widely regarded as the last large-scale <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">crusade</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, failed to stop the advance of the victorious Ottoman Turks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1045330069" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="sidebar sidebar-collapse nomobile vcard plainlist"><tbody><tr><th class="sidebar-title"><div class="sidebar-pretitle" style="margin: -0.2em 0; font-size:69%; font-weight:normal;">Part of <a href="/wiki/Category:History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Category:History of the Ottoman Empire">a series</a> on the</div></th>
</tr><tr>

<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tulip_Era_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Tulip Era in the Ottoman Empire">Tulip Era</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(1718â1730)</span></li></ul></div></div></td>

<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nizam-i_Djedid" title="Nizam-i Djedid">Nizam-i Djedid</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(late 18th and early 19th)</span></li>

</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-content">
<div class="sidebar-list mw-collapsible mw-collapsed"><div class="sidebar-list-title"><a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire">Dissolution</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(1908â1922)</span></div><div class="sidebar-list-content mw-collapsible-content" style="background:#eee">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era" title="Second Constitutional Era">2nd Constitutional Era</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(1908â1920)</span></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire_during_World_War_I" title="Ottoman Empire during World War I">World War I</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(1914â1918)</span></li>

</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="border-top:#aaa 1px solid; border-bottom:#aaa 1px solid;">
<a href="/wiki/Historiography_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Historiography of the Ottoman Empire">Historiography</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ghaza_thesis" title="Ghaza thesis">Ghaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_decline_thesis" title="Ottoman decline thesis">Decline</a>)</td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Template:History of the Ottoman Empire"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Template talk:History of the Ottoman Empire"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>As the Turks expanded into the Balkans, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sieges_of_Constantinople#Ottoman_Sieges" title="Sieges of Constantinople">conquest of Constantinople</a> became a crucial objective. The Ottomans had already wrested control of nearly all former Byzantine lands surrounding the city, but the strong defense of Constantinople's strategic position on the <a href="/wiki/Bosporus" title="Bosporus">Bosporus</a> Strait made it difficult to conquer. In 1402, the Byzantines were temporarily relieved when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turco-Mongol" title="Turco-Mongol">Turco-Mongol</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Timur</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Empire" title="Timurid Empire">Timurid Empire</a>, invaded Ottoman Anatolia from the east. In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ankara" title="Battle of Ankara">Battle of Ankara</a> in 1402, Timur defeated the Ottoman forces and took Sultan <a href="/wiki/Bayezid_I" title="Bayezid I">Bayezid I</a> as a prisoner, throwing the empire into disorder. The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Interregnum" title="Ottoman Interregnum">ensuing civil war</a>, also known as the <i>Fetret Devri</i>, lasted from 1402 to 1413 as Bayezid's sons fought over succession. It ended when <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_I" title="Mehmed I">Mehmed I</a> emerged as the sultan and restored Ottoman power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 363">:â363â</span></sup>
</p><p>The Balkan territories lost by the Ottomans after 1402, including Thessaloniki, Macedonia, and Kosovo, were later recovered by <a href="/wiki/Murad_II" title="Murad II">Murad II</a> between the 1430s and 1450s. On 10 November 1444, Murad repelled the <a href="/wiki/Crusade_of_Varna" title="Crusade of Varna">Crusade of Varna</a> by defeating the Hungarian, Polish, and <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachian</a> armies under <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_III_of_Poland" title="WÅadysÅaw III of Poland">WÅadysÅaw III of Poland</a> (also King of Hungary) and <a href="/wiki/John_Hunyadi" title="John Hunyadi">John Hunyadi</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Varna" title="Battle of Varna">Battle of Varna</a>, although Albanians under <a href="/wiki/Skanderbeg" title="Skanderbeg">Skanderbeg</a> continued to resist. Four years later, John Hunyadi prepared another army of Hungarian and Wallachian forces to attack the Turks, but was again defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo_(1448)" title="Battle of Kosovo (1448)">Second Battle of Kosovo</a> in 1448.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 29">:â29â</span></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Expansion_and_peak_.281453.E2.80.931566.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_and_peak_(1453â1566)">Expansion and peak (1453â1566)</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Classical_Age_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Classical Age of the Ottoman Empire">Classical Age of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1224" data-file-width="903" decoding="async" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg/170px-Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg/255px-Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg/340px-Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sultan <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror" title="Mehmed the Conqueror">Mehmed the Conqueror</a>'s entry into <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>; painting by <a href="/wiki/Fausto_Zonaro" title="Fausto Zonaro">Fausto Zonaro</a> (1854â1929)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs,_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3159" data-file-width="2160" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs%2C_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg/170px-Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs%2C_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs%2C_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg/255px-Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs%2C_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs%2C_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg/340px-Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs%2C_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs,_with_Suleiman_I_in_the_middle.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_miniature" title="Ottoman miniature">Ottoman miniature</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of MohÃ¡cs">Battle of MohÃ¡cs</a> in 1526<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[46]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The son of Murad II, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror" title="Mehmed the Conqueror">Mehmed the Conqueror</a>, reorganized both state and military, and on 29 May 1453 conquered <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">Constantinople</a>, ending the Byzantine Empire. Mehmed allowed the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> to maintain its autonomy and land in exchange for accepting Ottoman authority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-books.google-54">[47]</a></sup> Due to tension between the states of western Europe and the later Byzantine Empire, the majority of the Orthodox population accepted Ottoman rule as preferable to Venetian rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-books.google-54">[47]</a></sup> Albanian resistance was a major obstacle to Ottoman expansion on the Italian peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 15th and 16th centuries, the Ottoman Empire entered a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Growth_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Growth of the Ottoman Empire">period of expansion</a>. The Empire prospered under the rule of a line of committed and effective <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_Dynasty" title="Ottoman Dynasty">Sultans</a>. It also flourished economically due to its control of the major overland trade routes between Europe and Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 111">:â111â</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[h]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sultan <a href="/wiki/Selim_I" title="Selim I">Selim I</a> (1512â1520) dramatically expanded the Empire's eastern and southern frontiers by defeating <a href="/wiki/Ismail_I" title="Ismail I">Shah Ismail</a> of <a href="/wiki/Safavid_Iran" title="Safavid Iran">Safavid Iran</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chaldiran" title="Battle of Chaldiran">Battle of Chaldiran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 91â105">:â91â105â</span></sup> Selim I established <a href="/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet" title="Egypt Eyalet">Ottoman rule in Egypt</a> by defeating and annexing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo)" title="Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)">Mamluk Sultanate of Egypt</a> and created a naval presence on the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>. After this Ottoman expansion, competition began between the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> and the Ottoman Empire to become the dominant power in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 55â76">:â55â76â</span></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a> (1520â1566) captured <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> in 1521, conquered the southern and central parts of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Hungarian_Wars" title="OttomanâHungarian Wars">OttomanâHungarian Wars</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[53]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (February 2013)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> and, after his historic victory in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of MohÃ¡cs">Battle of MohÃ¡cs</a> in 1526, he established Ottoman rule in the territory of present-day Hungary (except the western part) and other Central European territories. He then laid <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Vienna_(1529)" title="Siege of Vienna (1529)">siege to Vienna</a> in 1529, but failed to take the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 50">:â50â</span></sup> In 1532, he made another <a href="/wiki/Habsburg%E2%80%93Ottoman_wars_in_Hungary_(1526%E2%80%931568)" title="HabsburgâOttoman wars in Hungary (1526â1568)">attack</a> on Vienna, but was repulsed in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_G%C3%BCns" title="Siege of GÃ¼ns">Siege of GÃ¼ns</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thompson442_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson442-63">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ãgoston_and_Alan_Masters583_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ãgoston_and_Alan_Masters583-64">[56]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, Wallachia and, intermittently, <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>, became tributary principalities of the Ottoman Empire. In the east, the Ottoman Turks <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Safavid_War_(1532%E2%80%931555)" title="OttomanâSafavid War (1532â1555)">took</a> <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> from the Persians in 1535, gaining control of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> and naval access to the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>. In 1555, the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> became officially partitioned for the first time between the Safavids and the Ottomans, a <i><a href="/wiki/Status_quo" title="Status quo">status quo</a></i> that would remain until the end of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1768%E2%80%931774)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1768â1774)">Russo-Turkish War (1768â1774)</a>. By this partitioning of the Caucasus as signed in the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Amasya" title="Peace of Amasya">Peace of Amasya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Armenia" title="Western Armenia">Western Armenia</a>, western <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan" title="Kurdistan">Kurdistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Imereti" title="Kingdom of Imereti">Western Georgia</a> (including western <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samtskhe-Atabagate" title="Samtskhe-Atabagate">Samtskhe</a>) fell into Ottoman hands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[57]</a></sup> while southern <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Armenia" title="Eastern Armenia">Eastern Armenia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Georgia" title="Eastern Georgia">Eastern Georgia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> remained Persian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1539, a 60,000-strong Ottoman army besieged the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Spain" title="Habsburg Spain">Spanish</a> garrison of <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Castelnuovo" title="Siege of Castelnuovo">Castelnuovo</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adriatic_coast" title="Adriatic coast">Adriatic coast</a>; the successful siege cost the Ottomans 8,000 casualties,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[59]</a></sup> but <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venice</a> agreed to terms in 1540, surrendering most of its empire in the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Morea" title="Morea">Morea</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Modern_France" title="Early Modern France">France</a> and the Ottoman Empire, united by mutual opposition to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> rule, became strong allies. The French conquests of <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Nice" title="Siege of Nice">Nice</a> (1543) and <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Corsica_(1553)" title="Invasion of Corsica (1553)">Corsica</a> (1553) occurred as a joint venture between the forces of the French king <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I</a> and Suleiman, and were commanded by the Ottoman admirals <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Hayreddin Barbarossa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dragut" title="Dragut">Dragut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[60]</a></sup> A month before the siege of Nice, France supported the Ottomans with an artillery unit during the 1543 Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Esztergom_(1543)" title="Siege of Esztergom (1543)">conquest of Esztergom</a> in northern Hungary. After further advances by the Turks, the Habsburg ruler <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor">Ferdinand</a> officially recognized Ottoman ascendancy in Hungary in 1547. <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman I</a> died of natural causes in his tent during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Szigetv%C3%A1r" title="Siege of SzigetvÃ¡r">Siege of SzigetvÃ¡r</a> in 1566.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:353px;max-width:353px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EmperorSuleiman.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2117" data-file-width="1810" decoding="async" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/EmperorSuleiman.jpg/180px-EmperorSuleiman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/EmperorSuleiman.jpg/270px-EmperorSuleiman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/EmperorSuleiman.jpg/360px-EmperorSuleiman.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:167px;max-width:167px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tizian_123.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="875" data-file-width="684" decoding="async" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tizian_123.jpg/165px-Tizian_123.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tizian_123.jpg/248px-Tizian_123.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Tizian_123.jpg/330px-Tizian_123.jpg 2x" width="165"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a> and his wife <a href="/wiki/Hurrem_Sultan" title="Hurrem Sultan">HÃ¼rrem Sultan</a>, two portraits by 16th century <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venetian</a> <a href="/wiki/Venetian_painting" title="Venetian painting">painter</a> <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>By the end of <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman</a>'s reign, the Empire spanned approximately 877,888Â sqÂ mi (2,273,720Â km<sup>2</sup>), extending over three continents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 545">:â545â</span></sup> In addition, the Empire became a dominant naval force, controlling much of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 61">:â61â</span></sup> By this time, the Ottoman Empire was a major part of the European political sphere. The Ottomans became involved in multi-continental religious wars when Spain and Portugal were united under the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a>. The Ottomans were holders of the Caliph title, meaning they were the leaders of all Muslims worldwide. The Iberians were leaders of the Christian crusaders, and so the two were locked in a worldwide conflict. There were zones of operations in the Mediterranean Sea<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[63]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[64]</a></sup> where Iberians circumnavigated Africa to reach India and, on their way, wage war upon the Ottomans and their local Muslim allies. Likewise, the Iberians passed through newly-Christianized <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Salcedo" title="Juan de Salcedo">had sent expeditions</a> that traversed the Pacific in order to Christianize the formerly Muslim <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and use it as a base to further attack the Muslims in the <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[65]</a></sup> In this case, the Ottomans sent armies to aid its easternmost vassal and territory, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Aceh" title="Sultanate of Aceh">Sultanate of Aceh</a> in Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 84">:â84â</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[67]</a></sup> During the 1600s, the worldwide conflict between the Ottoman Caliphate and Iberian Union was a stalemate <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_in_1600" title="List of countries by population in 1600">since both powers were at similar population, technology and economic levels.</a> Nevertheless, the success of the Ottoman political and military establishment was compared to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, despite the difference in the size of their respective territories, by the likes of the contemporary Italian scholar <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Sansovino" title="Francesco Sansovino">Francesco Sansovino</a> and the French political philosopher <a href="/wiki/Jean_Bodin" title="Jean Bodin">Jean Bodin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deringil709_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-deringil709-76">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Stagnation_and_reform_.281566.E2.80.931827.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stagnation_and_reform_(1566â1827)">Stagnation and reform (1566â1827)</span></h3>
<h4><span id="Revolts.2C_reversals.2C_and_revivals_.281566.E2.80.931683.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolts,_reversals,_and_revivals_(1566â1683)">Revolts, reversals, and revivals (1566â1683)</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transformation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Transformation of the Ottoman Empire">Transformation of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_Decline_Thesis" title="Ottoman Decline Thesis">Ottoman Decline Thesis</a></div>
<p>In the second half of the sixteenth century, the Ottoman Empire came under increasing strain from inflation and the rapidly rising costs of warfare that were impacting both Europe and the Middle East. These pressures led to a series of crises around the year 1600, placing great strain upon the Ottoman system of government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 413â414">:â413â414â</span></sup> The empire underwent a series of transformations of its political and military institutions in response to these challenges, enabling it to successfully adapt to the new conditions of the seventeenth century and remain powerful, both militarily and economically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-decline_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-decline-31">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 10">:â10â</span></sup> Historians of the mid-twentieth century once characterised this period as one of stagnation and decline, but this view is now rejected by the majority of academics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-decline_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-decline-31">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OttomanEmpireIn1683.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1850" data-file-width="1966" decoding="async" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/OttomanEmpireIn1683.png/310px-OttomanEmpireIn1683.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/OttomanEmpireIn1683.png/465px-OttomanEmpireIn1683.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/OttomanEmpireIn1683.png/620px-OttomanEmpireIn1683.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OttomanEmpireIn1683.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Ottoman territorial acquisitions up to 1683</div></div></div>
<p>The discovery of new maritime trade routes by Western European states allowed them to avoid the Ottoman trade monopoly. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portuguese</a> discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> in 1488 initiated <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_naval_expeditions_in_the_Indian_Ocean" title="Ottoman naval expeditions in the Indian Ocean">a series of Ottoman-Portuguese naval wars</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> throughout the 16th century. Despite the growing European presence in the Indian Ocean, Ottoman trade with the east continued to flourish. Cairo, in particular, benefitted from the rise of Yemeni coffee as a popular consumer commodity. As coffeehouses appeared in cities and towns across the empire, Cairo developed into a major center for its trade, contributing to its continued prosperity throughout the seventeenth and much of the eighteenth century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 507â508">:â507â508â</span></sup>
</p><p>Under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_IV" title="Ivan IV">Ivan IV</a> (1533â1584), the <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a> expanded into the Volga and Caspian region at the expense of the Tatar khanates. In 1571, the Crimean khan <a href="/wiki/Devlet_I_Giray" title="Devlet I Giray">Devlet I Giray</a>, commanded by the Ottomans, <a href="/wiki/Fire_of_Moscow_(1571)" title="Fire of Moscow (1571)">burned Moscow</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies2007_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davies2007-80">[72]</a></sup> The next year, the invasion was repeated but repelled at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Molodi" title="Battle of Molodi">Battle of Molodi</a>. The Ottoman Empire continued to invade Eastern Europe in a series of <a href="/wiki/List_of_conflicts_in_Europe_during_Turco-Mongol_rule" title="List of conflicts in Europe during Turco-Mongol rule">slave raids</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Subtelny2000_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Subtelny2000-81">[73]</a></sup> and remained a significant power in Eastern Europe until the end of the 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Ottomans decided to conquer <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Cyprus" title="Venetian Cyprus">Venetian Cyprus</a> and on 22 July 1570, Nicosia was besieged; 50,000 Christians died, and 180,000 were enslaved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 67">:â67â</span></sup> On 15 September 1570, the Ottoman cavalry appeared before the last Venetian stronghold in Cyprus, Famagusta. The Venetian defenders would hold out for 11 months against a force that would come to number 200,000 men with 145 cannons; 163,000 cannonballs struck the walls of Famagusta before it fell to the Ottomans in August 1571. The <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Famagusta" title="Siege of Famagusta">Siege of Famagusta</a> claimed 50,000 Ottoman casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 328">:â328â</span></sup> Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1571)" title="Holy League (1571)">Holy league</a> consisting of mostly Spanish and Venetian fleets won a victory over the Ottoman fleet at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Battle of Lepanto</a> (1571), off southwestern Greece; Catholic forces killed over 30,000 Turks and destroyed 200 of their ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 24">:â24â</span></sup> It was a startling, if mostly symbolic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979272_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979272-86">[78]</a></sup> blow to the image of Ottoman invincibility, an image which the victory of the Knights of Malta over the Ottoman invaders in the 1565 <a href="/wiki/Great_Siege_of_Malta" title="Great Siege of Malta">Siege of Malta</a> had recently set about eroding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[79]</a></sup> The battle was far more damaging to the Ottoman navy in sapping experienced manpower than the loss of ships, which were rapidly replaced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 53">:â53â</span></sup> The Ottoman navy recovered quickly, persuading Venice to sign a peace treaty in 1573, allowing the Ottomans to expand and consolidate their position in North Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198067_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198067-89">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>By contrast, the Habsburg frontier had settled somewhat, a stalemate caused by a stiffening of the Habsburg defenses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198071_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198071-90">[82]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Long_Turkish_War" title="Long Turkish War">Long Turkish War</a> against Habsburg Austria (1593â1606) created the need for greater numbers of Ottoman infantry equipped with firearms, resulting in a relaxation of recruitment policy. This contributed to problems of indiscipline and outright rebelliousness within the corps, which were never fully solved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198090â92_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198090â92-91">[83]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:AGE_MATTERS" title="Wikipedia:AGE MATTERS"><span title="This claim needs references to more current sources. (September 2016)">obsoleteÂ source</span></a></i>]</sup> Irregular sharpshooters (<a href="/wiki/Sekban" title="Sekban">Sekban</a>) were also recruited, and on demobilisation turned to <a href="/wiki/Brigandage" title="Brigandage">brigandage</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jelali_revolts" title="Jelali revolts">Jelali revolts</a> (1590â1610), which engendered widespread anarchy in <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> in the late 16th and early 17th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 24">:â24â</span></sup> With the Empire's population reaching 30Â million people by 1600, the shortage of land placed further pressure on the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979281_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979281-93">[85]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:AGE_MATTERS" title="Wikipedia:AGE MATTERS"><span title="This claim needs references to more current sources. (September 2016)">obsoleteÂ source</span></a></i>]</sup> In spite of these problems, the Ottoman state remained strong, and its army did not collapse or suffer crushing defeats. The only exceptions were campaigns against the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid dynasty</a> of Persia, where many of the Ottoman eastern provinces were lost, some permanently. This <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ottoman-Safavid_War_(1603%E2%80%931618)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ottoman-Safavid War (1603â1618) (page does not exist)">1603â1618</a> war eventually resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nasuh_Pasha" title="Treaty of Nasuh Pasha">Treaty of Nasuh Pasha</a>, which ceded the entire Caucasus, except westernmost Georgia, back into Iranian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Safavid" title="Safavid">Safavid</a> possession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[86]</a></sup> The treaty ending the <a href="/wiki/Cretan_War_(1645%E2%80%931669)" title="Cretan War (1645â1669)">Cretan War (1645â1669)</a> cost Venice much of <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Dalmatia" title="Venetian Dalmatia">Dalmatia</a>, its Aegean island possessions, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Candia" title="Kingdom of Candia">Crete</a>. (Losses from the war totalled 30,985 Venetian soldiers and 118,754 Turkish soldiers.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 33">:â33â</span></sup>
</p><p>During his brief majority reign, <a href="/wiki/Murad_IV" title="Murad IV">Murad IV</a> (1623â1640) reasserted central authority and recaptured <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> (1639) from the Safavids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198073_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198073-96">[88]</a></sup> The resulting <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Zuhab" title="Treaty of Zuhab">Treaty of Zuhab</a> of that same year decisively divided the Caucasus and adjacent regions between the two neighbouring empires as it had already been defined in the 1555 Peace of Amasya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Women" title="Sultanate of Women">Sultanate of Women</a> (1533â1656) was a period in which the mothers of young sultans exercised power on behalf of their sons. The most prominent women of this period were <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6sem_Sultan" title="KÃ¶sem Sultan">KÃ¶sem Sultan</a> and her daughter-in-law <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turhan_Hatice" title="Turhan Hatice">Turhan Hatice</a>, whose political rivalry culminated in KÃ¶sem's murder in 1651.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198074â75_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198074â75-99">[91]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6pr%C3%BCl%C3%BC_era" title="KÃ¶prÃ¼lÃ¼ era">KÃ¶prÃ¼lÃ¼ era</a> (1656â1703), effective control of the Empire was exercised by a sequence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" title="Grand Vizier">Grand Viziers</a> from the KÃ¶prÃ¼lÃ¼ family. The KÃ¶prÃ¼lÃ¼ Vizierate saw renewed military success with authority restored in Transylvania, the conquest of <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a> completed in 1669, and expansion into <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ukraine#PolishâLithuanian_Commonwealth" title="History of Ukraine">Polish southern Ukraine</a>, with the strongholds of <a href="/wiki/Khotyn" title="Khotyn">Khotyn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kamianets-Podilskyi" title="Kamianets-Podilskyi">Kamianets-Podilskyi</a> and the territory of <a href="/wiki/Podolia" title="Podolia">Podolia</a> ceding to Ottoman control in 1676.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198080â81_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198080â81-100">[92]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1842" data-file-width="2783" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg/220px-Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg/330px-Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg/440px-Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna" title="Battle of Vienna">Second Siege of Vienna</a> in 1683, by <a href="/wiki/Frans_Geffels" title="Frans Geffels">Frans Geffels</a> (1624â1694).</div></div></div>
<p>This period of renewed assertiveness came to a calamitous end in 1683 when Grand Vizier <a href="/wiki/Kara_Mustafa_Pasha" title="Kara Mustafa Pasha">Kara Mustafa Pasha</a> led a huge army to attempt a second Ottoman siege of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Vienna" title="History of Vienna">Vienna</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Turkish_War" title="Great Turkish War">Great Turkish War</a> of 1683â1699. The final assault being fatally delayed, the Ottoman forces were swept away by allied Habsburg, German, and Polish forces spearheaded by the Polish king <a href="/wiki/John_III_Sobieski" title="John III Sobieski">John III Sobieski</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna" title="Battle of Vienna">Battle of Vienna</a>. The alliance of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1684)" title="Holy League (1684)">Holy League</a> pressed home the advantage of the defeat at Vienna, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Karlowitz" title="Treaty of Karlowitz">Treaty of Karlowitz</a> (26 January 1699), which ended the Great Turkish War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979357_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979357-101">[93]</a></sup> The Ottomans surrendered control of significant territories, many permanently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198084_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198084-102">[94]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_II" title="Mustafa II">Mustafa II</a> (1695â1703) led the counterattack of 1695â1696 against the Habsburgs in Hungary, but was undone at the disastrous defeat at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Zenta" title="Battle of Zenta">Zenta</a> (in modern Serbia), 11 September 1697.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198083â84_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198083â84-103">[95]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_defeats">Military defeats</span></h4>
<p>Aside from the loss of the <a href="/wiki/Banat" title="Banat">Banat</a> and the temporary loss of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Belgrade" title="History of Belgrade">Belgrade</a> (1717â1739), the Ottoman border on the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a> remained stable during the eighteenth century. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expansion_of_Russia_1500%E2%80%931800" title="Expansion of Russia 1500â1800">Russian expansion</a>, however, presented a large and growing threat. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371-104">[96]</a></sup> Accordingly, King <a href="/wiki/Charles_XII_of_Sweden" title="Charles XII of Sweden">Charles XII of Sweden</a> was welcomed as an ally in the Ottoman Empire following his defeat by the Russians at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Poltava" title="Battle of Poltava">Battle of Poltava</a> of 1709 in central Ukraine (part of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a> of 1700â1721).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371-104">[96]</a></sup> Charles XII persuaded the Ottoman Sultan <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_III" title="Ahmed III">Ahmed III</a> to declare war on Russia, which resulted in an Ottoman victory in the <a href="/wiki/Pruth_River_Campaign" title="Pruth River Campaign">Pruth River Campaign</a> of 1710â1711, in Moldavia. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979372_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979372-105">[97]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG/220px-1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG/330px-1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG/440px-1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Austrian troops led by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Eugene_of_Savoy" title="Prince Eugene of Savoy">Prince Eugene of Savoy</a> captured <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> in 1717. Austrian control in Serbia lasted until the Turkish victory in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Russian%E2%80%93Turkish_War_(1735%E2%80%931739)" title="Austro-RussianâTurkish War (1735â1739)">Austro-RussianâTurkish War (1735â1739)</a>. With the 1739 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Belgrade" title="Treaty of Belgrade">Treaty of Belgrade</a>, the Ottoman Empire regained northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosnia" title="Bosnia">Bosnia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_(1718%E2%80%931739)" title="Kingdom of Serbia (1718â1739)">Habsburg Serbia</a> (including Belgrade), <a href="/wiki/Oltenia" title="Oltenia">Oltenia</a> and the southern parts of the <a href="/wiki/Banat_of_Temeswar" title="Banat of Temeswar">Banat of Temeswar</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Turkish_War_(1716%E2%80%931718)" title="Austro-Turkish War (1716â1718)">Austro-Turkish War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Passarowitz" title="Treaty of Passarowitz">Treaty of Passarowitz</a> confirmed the loss of the Banat, Serbia, and <a href="/wiki/Oltenia" title="Oltenia">"Little Walachia" (Oltenia)</a> to Austria. The Treaty also revealed that the Ottoman Empire was on the defensive and unlikely to present any further aggression in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979376_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979376-106">[98]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Russian%E2%80%93Turkish_War_(1735%E2%80%931739)" title="Austro-RussianâTurkish War (1735â1739)">Austro-RussianâTurkish War</a> (1735â1739), which was ended by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Belgrade" title="Treaty of Belgrade">Treaty of Belgrade</a> in 1739, resulted in the Ottoman recovery of northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosnia" title="Bosnia">Bosnia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_(1718%E2%80%931739)" title="Kingdom of Serbia (1718â1739)">Habsburg Serbia</a> (including Belgrade), <a href="/wiki/Oltenia" title="Oltenia">Oltenia</a> and the southern parts of the <a href="/wiki/Banat_of_Temeswar" title="Banat of Temeswar">Banat of Temeswar</a>; but the Empire lost the port of <a href="/wiki/Azov" title="Azov">Azov</a>, north of the Crimean Peninsula, to the Russians. After this treaty the Ottoman Empire was able to enjoy a generation of peace, as Austria and Russia were forced to deal with the rise of <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979392_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979392-107">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Science_and_Technology_in_the_Ottoman_Empire#Education" title="Science and Technology in the Ottoman Empire">Educational and technological reforms</a> came about, including the establishment of higher education institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Technical_University" title="Istanbul Technical University">Istanbul Technical University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[100]</a></sup> In 1734 an artillery school was established to impart Western-style artillery methods, but the Islamic clergy successfully objected under the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Theodicy" title="Theodicy">theodicy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google_a_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_a-109">[101]</a></sup> In 1754 the artillery school was reopened on a semi-secret basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google_a_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_a-109">[101]</a></sup> In 1726, <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Muteferrika" title="Ibrahim Muteferrika">Ibrahim Muteferrika</a> convinced the Grand Vizier <a href="/wiki/Nev%C5%9Fehirli_Damat_Ibrahim_Pasha" title="NevÅehirli Damat Ibrahim Pasha">NevÅehirli Damat Ibrahim Pasha</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Mufti" title="Grand Mufti">Grand Mufti</a>, and the clergy on the efficiency of the printing press, and Muteferrika was later granted by Sultan Ahmed III permission to publish non-religious books (despite opposition from some <a href="/wiki/Islamic_calligraphy" title="Islamic calligraphy">calligraphers</a> and religious leaders).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katip_celebi_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-katip_celebi-110">[102]</a></sup> Muteferrika's press published its first book in 1729 and, by 1743, issued 17 works in 23 volumes, each having between 500 and 1,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katip_celebi_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-katip_celebi-110">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-watson_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-watson-111">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="754" data-file-width="1130" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg/220px-January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg/330px-January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg/440px-January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ottoman troops attempting to halt the advancing Russians during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Ochakov_(1788)" title="Siege of Ochakov (1788)">Siege of Ochakov</a> in 1788</div></div></div>
<p>In North Africa, Spain <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Oran_(1732)" title="Spanish conquest of Oran (1732)">conquered Oran</a> from the autonomous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deylik_of_Algiers" title="Deylik of Algiers">Deylik of Algiers</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beylik_of_Oran" title="Beylik of Oran">Bey of Oran</a> received an army from Algiers, but it failed to recapture <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a>; the siege caused the deaths of 1,500 Spaniards, and even more Algerians. The Spanish also massacred many Muslim soldiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[104]</a></sup> In 1792, Spain abandoned Oran, selling it to the Deylik of Algiers.
</p><p>In 1768 Russian-backed Ukrainian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haidamaka" title="Haidamaka">Haidamakas</a>, pursuing Polish confederates, entered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balta,_Odessa_Oblast" title="Balta, Odessa Oblast">Balta</a>, an Ottoman-controlled town on the border of Bessarabia in Ukraine, massacred its citizens, and burned the town to the ground. This action provoked the Ottoman Empire into the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1768%E2%80%931774)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1768â1774)">Russo-Turkish War of 1768â1774</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_Kaynarca" title="Treaty of KÃ¼Ã§Ã¼k Kaynarca">Treaty of KÃ¼Ã§Ã¼k Kaynarca</a> of 1774 ended the war and provided freedom of worship for the Christian citizens of the Ottoman-controlled provinces of Wallachia and Moldavia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979405_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979405-113">[105]</a></sup> By the late 18th century, after a number of defeats in the wars with Russia, some people in the Ottoman Empire began to conclude that the reforms of <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a> had given the Russians an edge, and the Ottomans would have to keep up with Western technology in order to avoid further defeats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google_a_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_a-109">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Selim_III" title="Selim III">Selim III</a> (1789â1807) made the first major attempts to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_military_reform_efforts" title="Ottoman military reform efforts">modernise the army</a>, but his reforms were hampered by the religious leadership and the <a href="/wiki/Janissary" title="Janissary">Janissary</a> corps. Jealous of their privileges and firmly opposed to change, the Janissary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Janissary_revolts" title="Janissary revolts">revolted</a>. Selim's efforts cost him his throne and his life, but were resolved in spectacular and bloody fashion by his successor, the dynamic <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_II" title="Mahmud II">Mahmud II</a>, who <a href="/wiki/Auspicious_Incident" title="Auspicious Incident">eliminated the Janissary corps</a> in 1826.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_(1789).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2311" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg/220px-Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg/330px-Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg/440px-Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_(1789).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Selim_III" title="Selim III">Selim III</a> receiving dignitaries during an audience at the Gate of Felicity, <a href="/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace" title="TopkapÄ± Palace">TopkapÄ± Palace</a>. Painting by <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Kap%C4%B1da%C4%9Fl%C4%B1" title="Konstantin KapÄ±daÄlÄ±">Konstantin KapÄ±daÄlÄ±</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_revolution" title="Serbian revolution">Serbian revolution</a> (1804â1815) marked the beginning of an era of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_under_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Rise of nationalism under the Ottoman Empire">national awakening</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Question" title="Eastern Question">Eastern Question</a>. In 1811, the fundamentalist Wahhabis of Arabia, led by the al-Saud family, revolted against the Ottomans. Unable to defeat the Wahhabi rebels, the Sublime Porte had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt" title="Muhammad Ali of Egypt">Muhammad Ali Pasha</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kavala" title="Kavala">Kavala</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Wali" title="Wali">vali</a></i> (governor) of the <a href="/wiki/Egypt_Eyalet" title="Egypt Eyalet">Eyalet of Egypt</a>, tasked with retaking Arabia, which ended with the destruction of the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Diriyah" title="Emirate of Diriyah">Emirate of Diriyah</a> in 1818.
